<div id="review_128379643" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128379643" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128379643?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128379643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3682487026929712525"><i>Sometimes you must lose everything to find yourself.</i><br/> <br/>Jandy Nelson’s debut novel <b>The Sky is Everywhere</b> is an absolute must read for YA readers. I breezed through this book in one sitting, and I’m still going over in my heart and in my mind all the emotions this book made me feel about the complexities of grief and loss.<br/> <br/>Surprisingly enough, there were moments this book had me laughing out loud… literally guffawing and I’m not one prone to bursting out in hysterics, but Lennie’s analogies and ment</span>
  <span id="freeText3682487026929712525" style="display:none"><i>Sometimes you must lose everything to find yourself.</i><br /> <br />Jandy Nelson’s debut novel <b>The Sky is Everywhere</b> is an absolute must read for YA readers. I breezed through this book in one sitting, and I’m still going over in my heart and in my mind all the emotions this book made me feel about the complexities of grief and loss.<br /> <br />Surprisingly enough, there were moments this book had me laughing out loud… literally guffawing and I’m not one prone to bursting out in hysterics, but Lennie’s analogies and mental conflict, especially how she chose to express herself were truly hilarious at times. But at the same time, I’d become grounded and found myself sighing in sadness over her hurt and guilt. She took me along her journey of loss, confusion, betrayal, and self discovery; and refused to let go until she finished her story and went on her merry way. I was hooked on her every word and could probably listen to what she had to say for like ever! <br /> <br />Everything she shared about herself and her feelings served a purpose and not one word was wasted. In her own special way she came across as unintentionally funny, unabashedly snarky and unapologetically honest in what she expresses, feels and struggles with. She’s definitely a contender for my favorite female fictional character<br /> <br />In this book, Lennie shares her story of her life at seventeen immediately after the sudden and tragic death of her older sister Bailey. On her sister’s last day, Bailey was standing in their room bugging Lennie to share her opinion on what she should wear, and Lennie carelessly responded <i>I don’t care what you wear.</i> Those were the last words she ever spoke to her sister that she loved dearly. It made me think… how many times have I had a careless response like <i>I don’t care…</i> to one of my sisters? How would I feel if those were the last words I ever spoke to one of them??? But as Lennie showed us, in the same world where something as horrible as a sister dying, something as wonderful as falling in love can happen. This book hit close to home for me in so many ways it felt surreal.<br /><br />I just have to mention a few characters that surprisingly won me over quite quickly. I loved Lennie’s best friend Sarah. She’s loyal and honest and who wouldn’t love a girl who suffers from an ole macdonld’s version of turrets syndrome and sports shitkickers!?! I’ve recently acquired an immense liking for any characters that wear shitkickers. =) The other character I have to mention, is bat bat bat Joe. He was just full of awesomeness! Regardless of his reaction to a choice that Lennie made, I never lost hope in him that he’d eventually bring down his barrier and forgive. I struggled with Toby for a portion of the book, but one of the last scenes where Lennie found a special something at her sister’s grave site, made my heart ultimately ache for him. Those are just a few characters that I had to mention, but this story if filled with gems that will pull at your heartstrings the entire time and the ending is one that will leave you uplifted and filled with hope.<br /><br />Great book that I’m so glad I had the chance to experience, and one I have no reservations in recommending to others.<br /><br /><b>Favorite Quotes in the Book</b> <br /><br /><i>I’m huddled into the corner of the couch. I have no use for talking. I’d just as soon store paperclips in my mouth. - Lennie aka JL<br /> <br />It’s as if someone vacuumed up the horizon while we were looking the other way. - Lennie aka JL<br /> <br />Our tongues have fallen madly in love, gotten married and moved to Paris… Heathcliff and Cathy have nothing on us. - Lennie aka JL<br /> <br />I’ve never met anyone as heart broken as JL. I want to make her feel better.. want to be around her all the time… it’s crazy… it’s like she’s on full blast and everyone else is just on mute. - bat bat bat Joe<br /> <br />Each time someone dies, a library burns. - Anonymous<br /><br />My heart is yours.<br />I hear your soul in your music.<br />I belong to you.<br />- Lennie aka John Lennon</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3682487026929712525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

And this one for me was one of those truly great ones!   <span id="freeText954101261796059526" style="display:none">I always say that contemporary books are the hardest for me because it's hard for me to find a truly great one. And this one for me was one of those truly great ones! I adored every single emotional and quirky minute of it!<br /><br />I could so connect with Lennie's struggles and the stupid things she did at times, but they made sense why she did them. If I was in her position, I would have done them too! I love both Joe and Toby. They were just such great characters. Same goes for Big and Grams. I also loved the little written notes inside the book before some of the chapters! Seriously I'm super hungover from this one!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer5498556862644193422">tissue count: 7<br/><br/>this book was so freakin fantastic, one of my new favorites. <br/>like, up-at-1:30-AM-crying-because-it's-so-good favorite</span>

<div id="review_1711896267" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1711896267" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1711896267?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/30733884-the-sky-is-everywhere">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=romantic-recollections">romantic-recollections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=contemporary-cuteness">contemporary-cuteness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1711896267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5375949448281428753">This was breathtakingly beautiful and heartrendingly tragic read! I had (wrongfully) anticipated this to be a cute Summer read full of angsty teen romance and not much else.<br/><br/>The story follows Lennie Walker as she attempts to cope with teenage life and its many multiplying predicaments following the death of her big sister, Bailey.<br/><br/>I immediately felt an affinity and empathy with Lennie as, just two pages in, she professed her love for <i>Wuthering Heights</i>; my all-time favourite book! My love for this </span>
  <span id="freeText5375949448281428753" style="display:none">This was breathtakingly beautiful and heartrendingly tragic read! I had (wrongfully) anticipated this to be a cute Summer read full of angsty teen romance and not much else.<br /><br />The story follows Lennie Walker as she attempts to cope with teenage life and its many multiplying predicaments following the death of her big sister, Bailey.<br /><br />I immediately felt an affinity and empathy with Lennie as, just two pages in, she professed her love for <i>Wuthering Heights</i>; my all-time favourite book! My love for this fictional character only grew as we learn of her lonely depressive and dismal inner-most thoughts through the poetry she stashes around her town.<br /><br />Her beautiful soul was matched by the stunning and lyrical quality to the writing. I warmed to the entire story and could even forgive the emergence of the dreaded insta-love!<br /><br />Despite the touching subject-matter, there was levity and humour added to the text in the form of Lennie's Gram and Uncle Big. Her eccentric home life made me feel all fuzzy inside and I adored reading these sections especially.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5375949448281428753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7995609117674700285">The Soul Inside the Houseplant<br/><br/><br/>“Sometimes you must lose everything to find yourself“<br/><br/>Grandma, a six feet (tall) old lady who happens to be a guru on anything related to plants, is worried. She’s worried cos one of her plants is black-spotted and she’s trembling with the motive.<br/>That particular plant has a wireless connection to her granddaughter’s soul, reflecting her darkest feelings by means of colored stains:<br/><br/>Once it got white spots...<br/>Once it got brown spots...<br/><br/>However, both times, the girl and th</span>
  <span id="freeText7995609117674700285" style="display:none">The Soul Inside the Houseplant<br /><br /><br />“Sometimes you must lose everything to find yourself“<br /><br />Grandma, a six feet (tall) old lady who happens to be a guru on anything related to plants, is worried. She’s worried cos one of her plants is black-spotted and she’s trembling with the motive.<br />That particular plant has a wireless connection to her granddaughter’s soul, reflecting her darkest feelings by means of colored stains:<br /><br />Once it got white spots...<br />Once it got brown spots...<br /><br />However, both times, the girl and the plant perfectly recovered!<br />But this case seems more upsetting, cos black is the color of mourning plus the long line of sorrows that comes with it!...<br /><br />The Sky is Everywhere is a story about finding your own sky out of grief and self-discovery. This common premise turns into a story packed with magic characters, by the pen of Jandy Nelson. A story you’ll be reading like a real life fairy tale!<br /><br />“A secret: The kookiest elements of this novel are all true: The Spotted Plant, The Bad Luck House Purge, The Forest Bedroom, The Pyramids, and the biggie: A grief-stricken girl who scatters her poems all over town.”<br /><br />Jandy Nelson turns vapidity into poetry!<br />The Sky is Everywhere, and this book is also there — WOW😊😉🥰</span>

<div id="review_1025835539" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1025835539" />
    <a title="Lotte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25309949-lotte"><img alt="Lotte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408555448p2/25309949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1025835539?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lotte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lotte" href="/user/show/25309949-lotte">Lotte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142417805" href="/book/show/23168945-the-sky-is-everywhere">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=ge-ya-contemporary">ge-ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=2015-priority">2015-priority</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=a-young-adult-fiction">a-young-adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1025835539" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12474084626819981521">*3.5/5 stars.<br/>After I read <i>I'll Give You The Sun </i>last year and it easily became my favorite book of 2014, I obviously had high expectations for Jandy Nelson’s first book. And while this book met most of my expectations, it certainly didn’t exceed them.<br/>Let me explain: Basically, I just didn't like and couldn't sympathize with the main character Lennie. There are your typical immature and puberty stricken protagonists and then there’s Lennie. She definitely took it too far. Some decisions she made </span>
  <span id="freeText12474084626819981521" style="display:none">*3.5/5 stars.<br />After I read <i>I'll Give You The Sun </i>last year and it easily became my favorite book of 2014, I obviously had high expectations for Jandy Nelson’s first book. And while this book met most of my expectations, it certainly didn’t exceed them.<br />Let me explain: Basically, I just didn't like and couldn't sympathize with the main character Lennie. There are your typical immature and puberty stricken protagonists and then there’s Lennie. She definitely took it too far. Some decisions she made were just plain dumb.<br />My thought process while reading : "God no, Lennie! Don’t do that! Stop being so stupid!“ Then: "Ok, but she’s obviously grieving and has to go through a lot. She’ll probably learn from it.“ *Lennie does next stupid thing.* „Ok, nope.“. I just couldn’t get behind her logic.<br />(<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She scatters bits of texts and poems in public places all over her small town and then she's shocked that someone she knows finds them? Seriously?? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>)<br />However, the writing was just beautiful. The way Nelson can describe feelings makes them feel so immediate, real and poignant. I can only applaud her ability to do that! She just hits you in the feels. I also liked the way Lennie’s poems were integrated into the narrative. They really fluctuated in quality though - some of them were really gorgeous, while others felt a bit childish and clumsy.<br />I also enjoyed reading about all of the other characters that surrounded Lennie. I especially loved Sarah - she’s the kind of friend I’d like to have. Big and Gram were also very diverse and interesting characters.<br />The plot was rather predictable, which in the end didn’t bother me too much since this is not the kind of book that lives off shocking plot twists. However, my favorite YA contemporaries managed to build in great surprises into the character-driven narrative, and that just wasn’t the case in <i>The Sky is Everywhere</i>.<br />So,yeah. This wasn’t by any means a disappointment, but <i>I'll Give You The Sun</i> is superior in every way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12474084626819981521" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('i3icmXZ6O1WU8iFNzIlDm1uwOeXgmyIUIwoNqpD4Z7CxvYBLN6V0doodwmYqhYRpyYfT/skH2MsOhpamN080iA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('crvklW7u0U5CgODS5KRIUhfywaTy1BpuAt5dDSi4CM1IfvhHLzGebVxvA/kCqI+ghcUrv9tI4LEvUsYBjw9b9Q==')})
  }

Then Grace Town walks into his first period class on the third Tuesday of senior year and he knows everything\'s about to change.\n\nGrace isn\'t who Henry pictured as his dream girl-she walks with a cane, wears oversized boys\' clothes, and rarely seems to shower. She and Meg shared everything—so how was there no warning? But when Cody travels to Meg’s college town to pack up the belongings left behind, she discovers that there’s a lot that Meg never told her. About her old roommates, the sort of people Cody never would have met in her dead-end small town in Washington. About Ben McAllister, the boy with a guitar and a sneer, who broke Meg’s heart. And about an encrypted computer file that Cody can’t open—until she does, and suddenly everything Cody thought she knew about her best friend’s death gets thrown into question.  I Was Here is Gayle       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2982266.Jandy_Nelson">About Jandy Nelson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2982266.Jandy_Nelson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1429737179p3/2982266.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13728268889624836479">Jandy Nelson, like her characters in I’ll Give You the Sun and The Sky is Everywhere, comes from a superstitious lot. She was tutored from a young age in the art of the four-leaf clover hunt; she knocks wood, throws salt, and carries charms in her pockets. Her critically-acclaimed, New York Times bestselling second novel, I’ll Give You the Sun, received the prestigious Printz Award, Bank Street's </span>
  <span id="freeText13728268889624836479" style="display:none">Jandy Nelson, like her characters in I’ll Give You the Sun and The Sky is Everywhere, comes from a superstitious lot. She was tutored from a young age in the art of the four-leaf clover hunt; she knocks wood, throws salt, and carries charms in her pockets. Her critically-acclaimed, New York Times bestselling second novel, I’ll Give You the Sun, received the prestigious Printz Award, Bank Street's Josette Frank Award, and is a Stonewall Book Award honor. Both Sun and her debut, The Sky Is Everywhere, have been YALSA Best Fiction for Young Adults picks (Sun, a Top Ten on Both YALSA and Rainbow Lists) and on multiple best of the year lists including the New York Times, Time Magazine, NPR, have earned many starred reviews, and continue to enjoy great international success, collectively published in over 47 countries. I'll Give You the Sun has been sold to Warner Brothers and screenwriter Natalie Krinsky is currently writing the adaptation. Jandy, a literary agent for many years, received a BA from Cornell University and MFAs in Poetry and Children's Writing from Brown University and Vermont College of Fine Arts. Currently a full-time writer, she lives and writes in San Francisco, California—not far from the settings of her novels. Visit Jandy at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jandynelson.com">www.jandynelson.com</a>. Follow her on twitter: @jandynelson or Facebook: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://Facebook.com/jandy.nelson">Facebook.com/jandy.nelson</a>. Author photo credit: Sonya Sones.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13728268889624836479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
